mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[36]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
believe this means that the punishment of the damned will never end, or
others think at sometime in the future the configuration of the earth
and heaven will change.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn37" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref37" id="_ftn37"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[37]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Arab
legend is that the genii are the haughty or arrogant ones made from
“smokeless fire.”<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>However, they
may have just been a larger people or were more advanced in culture and
education, making them the “arrogant ones.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn38" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref38" id="_ftn38"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[38]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that the prophetess related the names of each of the eleven
stars, when she was questioned by a rabbi, who tried to entrap her as
being disgenuine.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn39" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref39" id="_ftn39"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[39]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Barbara,
a sister by the same mother.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn40" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref40" id="_ftn40"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[40]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
was said by some to be Judy, the most prudent and noble minded of them,
and some say that Miriam was the one that in fact told Judy to advise
her siblings not to kill Jacklyn, but to throw her into a pit privately,
intending to release her later.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>But then Judy persuaded the siblings to take her out of the pit
and sell her as a slave.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn41" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref41" id="_ftn41"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[41]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that the well was near Jerusalem, or was not far from the river
Jordan; but others call it the well of Egypt or Marain.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It is also said that when the siblings
of Jacklyn brought her into the field, they began to abuse and beat her
unmercifully.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>When she was thrown
into the well, she held onto some stones on the side.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The siblings had prior to this taken
off her inner garment at that time to show to their mother later.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Jacklyn begged to have her garment
returned to her, but her siblings said in a sneer that she should call
upon the eleven stars and the sun and the moon to rescue her or at least
keep her company.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Then they threw
her further down the well, whereupon she got up on a stone and the angel
Gabrielle came to her.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It is said
Jacklyn was 17 years old at the time. Some say that Gabrielle clothed
her in the well.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They say that
the garment at first belonged to Sarah, then when she was thrown into
fire by Nimrod, she was stripped, and then Gabrielle brought up the
garment and gave it to Jacklyn’s mother who had worn it as an amulet
about her neck, and Gabrielle was able to draw it out to give it to
Josie in the well.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn42" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref42" id="_ftn42"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[42]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Originally
a racing game for exercise to show dexterity in throwing darts, which is
still done in the East today.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn43" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref43" id="_ftn43"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[43]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Apparently
Josie thought this because while the garment was bloody, it was not
torn.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn44" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref44" id="_ftn44"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[44]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that Judy carried food to Jacklyn every day while she was in the
well, but on the fourth day she sold her to get her out of the well and
just told the other siblings that she was gone.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Some say that Jacklyn was sold
twice.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It is also said the name
of the person that found Jacklyn was Malec Ebn Dhor of the tribe
Khozaab.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Some say the person that
eventually bought Jacklyn was Kitfir, and he was superintendent of the
royal treasury, an important position.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn45" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref45" id="_ftn45"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[45]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that Jacklyn never seriously considered sleeping with her master,
while others say that she was enticed with his being very handsome, she
even went to far as to sit on his lap, and even began to undress
herself, when a voice called to her and said to beware of him; but she
took no notice until at length the angel Gabrielle called to her, or the
figure of the mistress of the home appeared, or her mother Jacklyn
appeared to her and bit her finger’s ends, whereupon her lust passed out
via her fingertips.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn46" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref46" id="_ftn46"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[46]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
woman’s name was Zoleikha.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The
women in the city referred to were 5 in number and wives of the king’s
chief officers, chamberlain, butler, baker, jailor and herdsman.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The women invited to the banquet were
40 in number.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn47" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref47" id="_ftn47"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[47]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Meaning
“life.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn48" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref48" id="_ftn48"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[48]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Holding
banquets was common among Egyptian women.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Learned women, or those that knew
poetry, or that could act and sing, were favorite entertainment.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn49" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref49" id="_ftn49"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[49]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
cutting of hands is said to be done between lovers, so show faith and
passion.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn50" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref50" id="_ftn50"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[50]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Perhaps
this was to cool the passion of Zoleikha’s husband, or to keep Jacklyn
away from her husband, or it was contrived by the husband to attempt to
force Jacklyn to surrender to his desires.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn51" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref51" id="_ftn51"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[51]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
number of years longer in prison may have been 7, 9, 10 or 12 years,
depending upon the commentator.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn52" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref52" id="_ftn52"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[52]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">To
protect it from weevils.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn53" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref53" id="_ftn53"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[53]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">At
this point, Jacklyn does not mention her former master, out of gratitude
for the favors received while in his house.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn54" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref54" id="_ftn54"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[54]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is related that once Jacklyn left prison, she was taken to the Queen,
whom she saluted in Hebrew, and the Queen asked what language that was,
she answered it was the language of her mothers.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>This Queen knew no less than 70
languages, and spoke with Jacklyn in each language, and Jacklyn was able
to answer her well in each language.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>The Queen marveled greatly, telling her of her dream, whereupon
Jacklyn answered all questions in the most minute detail.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>At that point, the Queen made Jacklyn
her Wazir or chief minister.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>At
about the same time, Jacklyn’s old master died, and one of his handsome
young sons married her, as he was a virgin and was young and pure to
her.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>She was, therefore, the same
woman who was called Asenath by Miriam.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn55" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref55" id="_ftn55"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[55]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is reported that Jacklyn, being made Wazir, governed with great
wisdom.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>She caused justice to be
impartially administered, and encouraged her people in industry and
agriculture during the seven years of plenty.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The natives to this day ascribe the
matriarch Jacklyn with almost all works of public utility, and in
particular, taking Feyyum from a standing pool or marsh to the most
fertile and best cultivated land in all of Egypt.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>In Syria and the neighboring
countries, the people were required to sell much of their possessions
and land, and many even became slaves to the Egyptians during the 7
years of drought, in order to survive.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>But after a period of time, Jacklyn released much of that back to
the depressed lands.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>During this
time, her siblings came to her to buy corn and said there were 11 of
them, but only 10 were present, whereupon Jacklyn asked where the
11<sup>th</sup> child was.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>But
they had no one to vouch for them, so Jacklyn sent them away with cattle
and with food and they drew lots to leave one sister, as a hostage for
payment.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Barbara was the sister
left behind.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn56" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref56" id="_ftn56"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[56]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Because
she was now a beautiful grown woman, finely dressed and made up.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn57" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref57" id="_ftn57"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[57]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">In
one legend it is said, that after Jacklyn had invited her siblings to
entertainment, she ordered them to be placed in pairs at a table for a
meal; upon which, upon having been placed to sit alone, Barbara burst
into tears, saying that if her sister were alive, she would have sat
with her.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Later, the siblings
were lodged in pairs again for the night, but Barbara slept in the same
room as Jacklyn.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Upon arising,
Jacklyn asked her whom she would have for a sister, if she could have
anyone in Jacklyn’s place, and Barbara replied that Jacklyn would have
made her an excellent sister, whereupon Jacklyn revealed her true
identity.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn58" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref58" id="_ftn58"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[58]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
relate this was a saa, or about a gallon measure.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Others believe it to have been a
precious gold or silver cup.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn59" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref59" id="_ftn59"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[59]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
person convicted of theft did not become a slave, but instead was
reduced to servitude for double the price of the item stolen.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn60" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref60" id="_ftn60"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[60]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
may be referring to Jacklyn either stealing a garment that once belonged
to Sarah, or she destroyed a negative idol of wealth made from gold that
belonged to her father.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn61" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref61" id="_ftn61"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[61]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said by some commentators that her pupils became white from weeping
and she lost part of her vision, but more likely this would have been
caused by cataracts because weeping alone does not cause
blindness.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn62" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref62" id="_ftn62"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[62]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Here
it is said that an angel told her that Jacklyn was still alive, perhaps
this occurred in a dream; others suppose it was based upon the prior
prediction that the siblings would bow down to Jacklyn during their
lives.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn63" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref63" id="_ftn63"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[63]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to the fact that the mother had sent a letter to Egypt begging for
Barbara’s release.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The siblings,
however did nothing about the fact that both Jacklyn and Barbara were
gone missing.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn64" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref64" id="_ftn64"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[64]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Apparently
the siblings recognized her either from her face and behavior, or from
her front teeth, or by taking off her crown, and discovering a mole on
her forehead.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn65" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref65" id="_ftn65"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[65]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Supposedly
this scent was carried on the wind a distance of 3 to 8 days.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn66" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref66" id="_ftn66"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[66]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that while only 72 women came into Egypt originally, by the time
Miriam left Egypt with the Jewish families, there were by then 600,500
men and women, besides the elderly and children.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn67" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref67" id="_ftn67"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[67]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is told that Jacklyn lived in Egypt twenty four years, and at her death,
she was to be buried in Palestine next to her mother.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Jacklyn returned to Palestine and died
twenty three years after that.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>But disputes arose among the Egyptians concerning her burial and
they even came to blows.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>At
length they agreed to put her body into a marble coffin, and sink it
into the Nile, to increase the flow of the river, thereby preventing
famine.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>But when Miriam led her
people out of Egypt, she exhumed the coffin and carried Jacklyn’s bones
to Canaan where they were buried with their foremothers.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn68" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref68" id="_ftn68"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[68]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Here
a distinction is made between those that live in the cities as being
generally more compassionate, more educated, while those that lived in
the desert were more ignorant and hard hearted.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn69" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref69" id="_ftn69"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[69]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">May
mean “I am the most wise and knowing Goddess” and is often interpreted
as this.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn70" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref70" id="_ftn70"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[70]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">As
in sweet and sour, black and white, smooth and rough, etc.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn71" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref71" id="_ftn71"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[71]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
has been changed from the original.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>Old Arab stories relate that an unbeliever goes to hell with a
heavy collar or neck weights around their necks, which consist of all
their evil deeds on earth.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Of
course this does not happen; the dark souls are merely recycled back to
earth.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn72" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref72" id="_ftn72"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[72]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Rain
in a desert land raises hope for crops and drinking water.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn73" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref73" id="_ftn73"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[73]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is believed to be a reference to the fact that shadows are so long in
the morning and evening that they appear to prostrate themselves before
Goddess.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn74" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref74" id="_ftn74"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[74]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
does not mean that the blind or deaf are lesser people or should be
mistreated.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>This is clearly an
allegory.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn75" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref75" id="_ftn75"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[75]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">By
committing suicide, engaging in drug or alcohol additions or other
extreme negative behaviors. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn76" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref76" id="_ftn76"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[76]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">As
Goddess is joined to God, and as all the prophetesses are joined
together, as husband and wife are joined together, etc. To refer to God
is the same as referring to Goddess and vice versa.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>For “God” is within “Goddess” and
“man” is within “woman.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn77" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref77" id="_ftn77"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[77]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
Koreish wanted the prophetess<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>to
prove her divinity by doing the following: move the mountains from Mecca
and put in gardens instead, have the wind transport them with their
goods to Syria, or have the earth cleaved in two, raise to life dead
prophetesses.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn78" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref78" id="_ftn78"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[78]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is referring to the point that some evil people and their followers
constantly annoyed and harassed the evil idolaters by plundering their
caravans and driving off their cattle</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span></span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">A true
prophetess would never teach hate or violence against others.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn79" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref79" id="_ftn79"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[79]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
would be referring to the ancient pagans, Arabs, Jews and Christians
that the prophetess was preaching to.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn80" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref80" id="_ftn80"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[80]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
was in response to some Jews that thought that a prophetess should not
have a spouse or children to distract her from her religious
duties.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Also, some felt that
sexual pleasures were incompatible with piousness and purity.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn81" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref81" id="_ftn81"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[81]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Thus,
made their paths in life easier for them to follow, rather than
wandering about like the unbelievers.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn82" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref82" id="_ftn82"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[82]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">See
Table B, Introduction, page x for some possible meanings of these
initials.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn83" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref83" id="_ftn83"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[83]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">At
that time, the Jewish population in Egypt was said to be very large, so
baby girls were killed at the time of birth, to prevent further
population growth.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The males were
not generally allowed to marry Egyptian women, and were used for heavy
slave work only.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn84" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref84" id="_ftn84"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[84]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Although
goddesses of peace and love were allowed as facets of the One True
Goddess named Allat, this was not what the dark entities wanted; they
wanted greed, war, hate and violence.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>They wanted to murder whomever they wanted and charge for goods
and services what they wanted in times of scarcity.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They did not believe in alms or
charitable acts, and they excluded others from their lands that they
deemed to be different from them, and also they would warmonger with
others, inciting hate and violence in the land.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They were nasty and violent and did
not want a prophetess that preached of a Goddess that was pure
love.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn85" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref85" id="_ftn85"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[85]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is probably referring to the Meccans, who felt they were blessed because
they had been given the Caaba and the control of it, and they also had
been given the mission of the prophetess, yet despite all of this, they
eventually became obstinate unbelievers, for which they were punished by
a famine of 7 years, but also by the loss and disgrace by losing at
Bedr.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn86" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref86" id="_ftn86"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[86]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is referring to the fact that Sarah had a husband, Abraham, and a slave,
Hagar.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>While her first daughter
Isabel was that of her husband, the second, Iris was that of her
slave.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Because her husband could
not be faithful to her, Sarah divorced Abraham and he left with Hagar
and Iris to live in the desert.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>They settled in a poorer valley for awhile, but Abraham
eventually returned to Sarah and found a second husband for Hagar.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>He was faithful after
that.</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
10.0pt"> </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn87" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref87" id="_ftn87"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[87]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to the people of Ada and Thelma, where their towns had been destroyed,
and the only ones that were saved were the believers that understood the
warning signs of the impending disaster.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn88" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref88" id="_ftn88"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[88]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
believe that the earth will turn white and the heavens will turn gold at
the end of the earth time.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn89" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref89" id="_ftn89"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[89]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Al
Hejr is a place, between Medina and Syria where the people of Thelma
lived and is mentioned near the end of the chapter.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn90" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref90" id="_ftn90"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[90]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">See
Table B, Introduction, page x.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn91" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref91" id="_ftn91"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[91]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Constellations
representing signs of the Zodiac.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn92" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref92" id="_ftn92"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[92]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
Arabs believed that devils inhabited the constellations in order to pry
into the actions and conversations of the inhabitants of heaven in order
to tempt them.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They also believed
that the evil spirits could enter into any of the seven heavens up until
the birth of Yeshua, and at that time, they could enter only three of
them, but were forbidden the other four.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn93" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref93" id="_ftn93"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[93]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
Arabs believe that when a star seems to fall or shoot, this is actually
the angels shooting away at evil spirits to keep them away from
heaven.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn94" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref94" id="_ftn94"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[94]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
could be referring to soldiers that stay behind in battle, or it could
refer to when people are born and when they die, or it may be referring
to a certain story when a beautiful woman came to prayer, some men would
come early and then stay late.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn95" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref95" id="_ftn95"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[95]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Note
this is a parable because Goddess does not curse anyone or anything, She
is pure love.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn96" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref96" id="_ftn96"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[96]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is not know whether they were fearful due to their strange appearance,
or coming at an unreasonable time, or else their not eating with
her.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn97" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref97" id="_ftn97"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[97]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Violent
and hateful.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn98" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref98" id="_ftn98"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[98]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Believed
by most to be the first seven verses, or Chapter 1, of the Korana;
believed by some to be the first full seven full chapters of the
Korana.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn99" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref99" id="_ftn99"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[99]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
interpret this as the “obstructors” or those that would prevent people
from entering the temple at Mecca, that they would be prevented from
embracing Islama.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn100" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref100" id="_ftn100"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[100]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">A
bee is mention approximately mid-chapter.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn101" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref101" id="_ftn101"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[101]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
person intended in this section was Obba Ebn Khalf who came to the
prophetess<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>with a rotten bone and
asked if it were possible for Goddess to resurrect that.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn102" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref102" id="_ftn102"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[102]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
creation of fresh edible fish from salt water was considered a
miracle.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn103" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref103" id="_ftn103"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[103]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Ancient
Arabs believed that the earth, when first created, was smooth and equal
and therefore liable to a circular motion like the celestial orbs they
studied, and when the angels asked who could stand on such a tottering
frame, Goddess fixed it the next morning by throwing the mountains upon
it.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn104" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref104" id="_ftn104"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[104]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
believe that this passage is referring to the Tower of Babel, which was
built for the purpose of ascending to heaven and waging war on the
occupants. It is said to have been built by Nimrod, the grandson of
Caanan, the son of Ham.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The tower
was subsequently destroyed by a violent wind and earthquake.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn105" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref105" id="_ftn105"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[105]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, the shadow is contracted while prostrate during worship.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn106" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref106" id="_ftn106"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[106]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that the ancient Arabs often buried baby daughters, but this is
a fairly absurd claim considering the fact the Arabs were polygynistic
and so many girls would have been required for every man–a difficult
task considering the maternal mortality rate.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Only during periods of war were there
generally more women than men However, many anthropologists now believe
that it was a common occurrence in times past to gain converts
to</span><span style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Lucida Sans Unicode&quot;;mso-bidi-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">
</span><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">a new religion by claiming that other or old
religions practiced devil worship, or infanticide, or temple sex–claims
that could often be discounted by historical evidence to the
contrary.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Unfounded rumors, it
seems, were often the fastest traveling news and they did in fact
effectively result in converting ancient peoples to various
religions.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn107" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref107" id="_ftn107"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[107]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is argued that it is ironic that the people were so willing to worship
many male deities, when they themselves found the birth of a baby boy to
be shameful and desired to bury it because they were so difficult and so
very hard to raise.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Further, they
might bring shame on the family if they engaged in acts of violence, or
raped a young girl or made one pregnant.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>Accordingly, this preacher is arguing should be the same for the
“sons of God,” as it is for their own sons.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>However, the better argument is that
Goddess does not bear children as human women do.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn108" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref108" id="_ftn108"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[108]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Honey
can be of various colors–red, black, yellow, white, according to the
plants the bee feeds upon.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It
should be considered a miracle that a bitter plant can produce a sweet
nectar in its flower, and an ever sweet substance of honey.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn109" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref109" id="_ftn109"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[109]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">There
is told a legend wherein a woman came to the prophetess with a stomach
ache and the prophetess told her to go and eat honey, which she
did.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>But the woman’s<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>stomach ache did not get better, so
she went back to the prophetess and she said to take more honey.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>After the woman did this, she did
recover right away.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn110" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref110" id="_ftn110"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[110]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Changed
from the original where it said that the wealthy do not share with their
slaves when they could make them equals.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn111" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref111" id="_ftn111"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[111]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
prophetess was admonishing the wealthy who would give freely to others,
but neglect their own slaves.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn112" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref112" id="_ftn112"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[112]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
liken this parable to Goddess and other minor deities, or the faithful
versus the unfaithful.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn113" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref113" id="_ftn113"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[113]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Originally
“in war,” but since war mongering is no longer permitted, the more
appropriate term is “dangerous situations.</span><span
style="font-family:
&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn114" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref114" id="_ftn114"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[114]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Apparently
the prophetess knew a woman who was a perfectionist and she would knit
or weave a garment during the day and then undo it at night believing it
was not good enough, only to start over the next day.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn115" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref115" id="_ftn115"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[115]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">One
story is told that, after reading the Korana, the prophetess uttered
something blasphemous, after which, she declared that Evil made her do
it.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>After this, prior to reading
or reciting the Korana many Muslimas repeat these words, “I have
recourse unto Goddess for assistance against Satan driven away with
stones.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn116" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref116" id="_ftn116"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[116]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">At
the time, there was much speculation and rumor that the Korana was not
actually channeled by the prophetess from the angel Gabrielle, but it
was forged by a number of suspects, too many to mention here.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The accusations of forgery and the
denouncement of this in the Korana is readily found at length on the
internet and need not be dealt with in this Book which is being
presented as a Book of faith, peace and love.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn117" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref117" id="_ftn117"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[117]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
stories that are told regarding these passages are based upon the
Koreish that would abduct the Moslemas and torment them until they
renounced their faith.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>In one
particular instance, numerous people were abducted, and in particular
one woman was tied between two camels and she was speared through her
private parts.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Many of the others
who watched this display immediately renounced their faith, but later
returned to the prophetess weeping, whereupon she forgave them and
published these verses.</span>

<span style="font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;"><span
style="mso-tab-count:
1">            </span>Even so, it was considered better to be severely
tortured than to renounce one’s faith.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>In one instance a Khoaib Ebn Ada was sold to the Koreish and was
then mutilated by the cutting off of pieces of his flesh.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>He was asked in the middle of his
torture, whether he wished that the prophetess was in his place and he
answered “I would not wish to be with my family, my substance, my
children, on condition that the prophetess was only to be pricked with a
thorn.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn118" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref118" id="_ftn118"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[118]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">May
be some or all of the following: putting Isaiah to death, imprisoning of
Jeremiah, slaying of Zachariah and John the Baptist and/or imaging the
death of Yeshua.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn119" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref119" id="_ftn119"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[119]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to the destruction of the Jewish Temple</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Lucida Sans Unicode&quot;;
mso-bidi-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;">.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn120" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref120" id="_ftn120"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[120]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
was to scold those Arabs that squandered away one’s substance in folly
or luxury, considered to be a very great sin.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Often they would kill camels and
distribute the food out of vanity and ostentation.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The prophetess forbid them to do this
and to take care of their poorer relations.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn121" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref121" id="_ftn121"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[121]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Two
types of trees determine good from evil.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>The Zakkum tree indicates evil because it is ugly, <span
style="mso-spacerun:yes"> </span>produces little shade and bears bitter
small fruits in scarcity, and this is distinguished from the shade trees
of paradise which form beautiful large canopies and produce abundant
sweet fruits.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn122" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref122" id="_ftn122"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[122]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is pure allegory; angels are not evil for they are pure love, just as
Goddess is.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn123" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref123" id="_ftn123"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[123]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Not
blind literally, but blind as to faith.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn124" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref124" id="_ftn124"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[124]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
supposedly is when a certain tribe came to the prophetess and asked if
they could join her religion on the condition that certain obligations
be waived, such as the giving of alms, frequent prayer, to keep Allat,
etc.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn125" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref125" id="_ftn125"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[125]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that when the prophetess entered the temple at Mecca that there
were 360 statutes, most of them negative male deities, and all she had
to say was “Truth has come, and falsehood has vanished” and the statutes
appear to topple over with just the touch of a stick.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Although these false negative deities
were a problem circa 625 CE, the use of images and statutes should not
present a problem now, as long as they are positive ones and not
predominately males ones either.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn126" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref126" id="_ftn126"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[126]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">One
Rabbi asked the prophetess to tell the details of the story of the cave
together with information about the human spirit, and the prophetess had
to admit she did not know this.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn127" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref127" id="_ftn127"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[127]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
legend of the cave is explained in the first few verses.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn128" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref128" id="_ftn128"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[128]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">In
the story of the cave, a certain number of persecuted Christians hid in
a cave and fell asleep for a number of years, until the reign of
persecution passed.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The number of
years of sleep varies from legend to legend.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn129" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref129" id="_ftn129"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[129]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
Moslemas hold this dog in very high esteem and it is said there is a
special place in heaven for him.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn130" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref130" id="_ftn130"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[130]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, they were looking for a miracle such as this one.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn131" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref131" id="_ftn131"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[131]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
people believe that the ruler referred to was Dhu’lkarnein or Alexander
the Great who was also referred to as the “two-horned.”<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Perhaps this is because he was king of
the East and the West, or because he made excursions to both parts of
the world, or because he had two horns on his diadem, or two curls of
hair, like horns on his forehead.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn132" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref132" id="_ftn132"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[132]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is told these people had neither clothes nor houses, their country did
not have any buildings, but the people lived in holes under ground,
where they retreated from the heat of the sun.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They may have been the Zenj, a black
nation lying southwest of Ethiopia.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>Or they may have been the troglodytes of the ancients.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn133" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref133" id="_ftn133"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[133]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">According
to infoplease.com, Gog and Magog are two nations led by Satan in a
climactic battle at Armageddon against the Queendom of Goddess.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Revelations<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>20.8</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn134" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref134" id="_ftn134"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[134]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is further related that the wall was built in this manner. <span
style="mso-spacerun:yes"> </span>It was dug until they found water, and
having laid the foundation of stone and melted brass, they build the
super structure of large pieces of iron, between which they laid wood
and coals, until they equaled the height of the mountains; then they set
fire to the combustibles, by the help of large bellows, they made the
iron red hot and over it poured melted brass, which filled up the spaces
between the pieces of iron, rendering the work as firm as a rock.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Others say the entire structure was
built of stone joined by pieces of iron upon which was poured melted
brass to fasten them together. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn135" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref135" id="_ftn135"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[135]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
possible meanings for these initials is given in Table C, Introduction,
page x.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn136" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref136" id="_ftn136"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[136]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said by some that she was so elevated that she could hear Goddess’
pen creaking as it wrote down decrees in heaven.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn137" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref137" id="_ftn137"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[137]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">She
was so blessed, she wrote down 30 Books of divine inspiration, and it is
said that she was the first who wrote with a pen, and who studied the
sciences of astronomy and arithmetic, etc.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn138" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref138" id="_ftn138"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[138]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Tales
are told that she was taken up directly by Goddess into heaven at the
age of 350, after having suffered death and been resurrected, and that
she is alive in one of the 7 heavens.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn139" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref139" id="_ftn139"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[139]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that the believers will have to walk through hell, but they will not
come near it, perhaps by passing over a narrow bridge over it, or by
having the flames dampened as they near it.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn140" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref140" id="_ftn140"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[140]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Changed
from the original where the unbelievers will appear alone and naked on
the day of the resurrection.</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;"></span>

</div>

</div>
